20/10/2019, 08:38 - Jenit Jain: So what's happening in fig a is that after wxa there's a rxa in p2, and we know that rxa will always follow wxa so that's why there's an arrow. 
Then wxb follows rxa, so rxb in p3 follows wxb. But rxa in p4 is independent of the other processes so we can say it's getting it's value from p1's wxa. And the rxb in p4 can follow.  But there's nothing for rxa in p3 because after rxb in p3, we know rxa can't happen (since x=b not a)
20/10/2019, 08:39 - Jenit Jain: And in the figb,
